Unlock the power of personalized medicine.

Transform preventive healthcare with polyvar's polygenic risk analysis reports. We make complex insights simple.

How does it work?

Our scores provide a comprehensive assessment of an individual's genetic predisposition to impactful diseases.

There are two options to obtain polygenic risk scores for a patient. You can either have the patient upload their 23andMe, Ancestry, or other such genetic sequencing data, or you can order one of our test kits. Our end-to-end pipeline takes care of the rest, performing an in-depth analysis on a plethora of genetic variants to determine their overall contribution to the risk profile.

Once the score is determined, our reporting makes it easy to understand the results.

We don't want cost or insurance to be a barrier to precision insights: this service is free, unless a sequencing kit needs to be ordered.

Inquire about testing our coronary artery disease report

Quality scores. More information.

  • Most complex traits and many disorders are polygenic. Each variant by itself has a minuscule effect, but thousands of these variants together makes a large effect.
  • Some scores we are able to generate include:
    • Obesity
    • Coronary artery disease
    • Extremely high or low blood pressure
    • Cancer
    • Anorexia nervosa
    • Externalizing disorders
    • Educational challenges
    • Intellectual disability
    • Asthma
    • Migraine
    • Irritable bowel syndrome
    • Type 1 and 2 diabetes
    • Alzheimer’s disease
    • Ankylosing Spondylitis
    • Schizophrenia
    • Rheumatoid Arthritis
    • Polycystic ovary syndrome
    • Many others






     

A sample of polygenic our scores offered

Breast cancer

Applying breast cancer polygenic scores in a risk model yeilds more effective identification of high-risk individuals.

Coronary artery disease

Polygenic scores can indicate if an individual is at high risk for coronary artery disease, indicating lifestyle changes or certain therapies may be particularly important compared to low polygenic risk individuals.
